  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ae8fc942-f7dc-4056-9a9a-d2eab1fe234a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7781827187130113241" style="display:none">I have been in love with Titus Oates for quite a while now--which is ridiculous, since he's been dead for ninety years. But look at it this way. In ninety years I'll be dead, too, and the age difference won't matter.<br /><br />Sym is not your average teenage girl. She is obsessed with the Antarctic and the brave, romantic figure of Captain Oates from Scott's doomed expedition to the South Pole. In fact, Oates is the secret confidant to whom she spills all her hopes and fears.<br /><br />But Sym's uncle Victor is even more obsessed--and when he takes her on a dream trip into the bleak Antarctic wilderness, it turns into a nightmarish struggle for survival that will challenge everything she knows and loves.<br /><br />In her first contemporary young adult novel, Carnegie Medalist and three-time Whitbread Award winner Geraldine McCaughrean delivers a spellbinding journey into the frozen heart of darkness.</span>

        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_132534319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132534319" />
    <a title="kwesi 章英狮" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi"><img alt="kwesi 章英狮" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549853625p2/4218875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132534319?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kwesi 章英狮" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kwesi 章英狮" href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi">kwesi 章英狮</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060890377" href="/book/show/6681612-the-white-darkness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=geraldine-mccaughrean">geraldine-mccaughrean</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer132534319&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132534319" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6858943550738670813">Do you have any idea how to live in a freezing dessert called South Pole? Or have you tried reading thousands of books regarding South Pole and the failed expedition of Captain Oates? What if you fall in love to an imaginary character just by watching an old film about South Pole? This book is sympathetically all you need to live in the South. No need for maps or self-help books and most of the entire journey is effortless.<br/><br/>I never wished to go to the South and I don’t have any idea how to fall i</span>
  <span id="freeText6858943550738670813" style="display:none">Do you have any idea how to live in a freezing dessert called South Pole? Or have you tried reading thousands of books regarding South Pole and the failed expedition of Captain Oates? What if you fall in love to an imaginary character just by watching an old film about South Pole? This book is sympathetically all you need to live in the South. No need for maps or self-help books and most of the entire journey is effortless.<br><br>I never wished to go to the South and I don’t have any idea how to fall in love to an imaginary character. This thing only happened to social declined people, I’m not insulting but that’s how the book described the character. When I was young, I never have an imaginary friend to play with all I have are real kids who wants to play <i>karate</i> and <i>Power Rangers</i>. <br><br>Imagine how old I was when those types of games were still on its peak, now kids have to sit and play with their play station or PSP. Life is too short guys, why not enjoy it outdoor? Scared of the sun? Well, go to the South and play with <i>Sym Wates</i> who enjoyed clinging with her imaginary boyfriend.<br><br><i>The White Darkness</i> is the story of <i>Sym Wates</i> who enjoyed watching and reading books related to South Pole, and have a relationship with an imaginary character. Quite disgusting for a lady character and interesting for a 14-year-old girl who enjoyed that kind of stuff. Because of her love to her uncle <i>Victor</i>, who taught her everything she needed to survive in the cold and taught her everything about books, she was mesmerized of her opportunity to go to the South because of her uncle’s stupidity about Inner World. <br><br>When they arrived to the South Pole, life turns upside-down, everything changed into frozen dreams. <i>Sym</i>’s beliefs will change forever as the story progress, until she knew the true meaning of oneself and the true meaning of love. Love not only to benefits others but to posses the power of judgment. Whatever happened to her in the end, I never cared to know it anymore.<br><br>The true motif of this book is to portray the abuse and the deception that her Uncle did to her since she was young, imagine she was forced to dream like him, she was fooled about her parents and lastly she was planned by her uncle to destroy her father. In this way her dillusional problem about her imaginary boyfriend was applied in the story and most of the children who have abused have this kind of psychological disorder.<br><br>The thing that did not work for me is that this book is to disgusting, okay, I’m not here to judge the characters. But I can’t imagine having a relationship with an imaginary boyfriend. Second, the sentences, the words and her style did not work well. It was like talking to yourself than to know the true essence of the book.<br><br>It took me hours or more than what I expected to finish this book. You have to read it well, read it slowly to understand it. The book also mentioned the true meaning of the title, although it was vividly explained, I can’t still get the whole point. But describing it as the mist of the South Pole and the treacherous natural characteristic of the place which I don’t have any idea since I never been there before.<br><br>This book was awarded by <i>Printz Award</i> in 2008 and so far I did not appreciate this. I recommend this book to young readers who enjoyed reading South Pole related stuff. This can be also enjoyed by mystery and adventure book lovers and lastly, those kids who have the same boyfriend like <i>Sym</i>. Enjoy reading! <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341867i/697856.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <i>The aurora australis snakes across the South Pole sky in 2002 in displays whose beauty awed researchers spending the winter there. (Photo courtesy of the U.S. Antarctic Program)</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Review posted on <b>
  <a href="http://oldfashionedreader.blogspot.com/2011/07/white-darkness-by-geraldine-mccaughrean.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Old-Fashioned Reader</a>
</b>.<br><br><b>Rating</b>: <i>The White Darkness</i> by Geraldine McCaughrean, <b>3 Sweets</b><br><br><b>Challenges</b>:<br><i>Book #205 for 2011</i><br><i>Book #120 for <a href="http://bareadingchallenges.blogspot.com/p/off-shelf-challenge.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Off the Shelf!</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6858943550738670813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_13345032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13345032" />
    <a title="Abby Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson"><img alt="Abby Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484521399p2/53329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13345032?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby Johnson" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson">Abby Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Abby by: </span>
      Printz award winner
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13345032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6389821231743933705">So many people have loved this book... I think it's just not my thing. After the death of her father, 14-year-old Symone, excruciatingly shy hearing-impaired geek with an imaginary friend, is whisked away on a surprise trip to Antarctica by her Uncle Victor. From the start you can sense that something's not right here. Victor's acting fishy, lying to Sym about their destination, stealing her mother's passport so she can't come with them... and things just get bleaker and bleaker as the journey g</span>
  <span id="freeText6389821231743933705" style="display:none">So many people have loved this book... I think it's just not my thing. After the death of her father, 14-year-old Symone, excruciatingly shy hearing-impaired geek with an imaginary friend, is whisked away on a surprise trip to Antarctica by her Uncle Victor. From the start you can sense that something's not right here. Victor's acting fishy, lying to Sym about their destination, stealing her mother's passport so she can't come with them... and things just get bleaker and bleaker as the journey goes on. <br /><br />My frustration is that Sym is so blinded by admiration for her Uncle (who's actually just a close family friend, not a blood relative), that she can't see that things are horribly wrong. I kept waiting for her to take charge and save the day (or at least save herself), but she just kept going with the flow as things got worse and worse... Also, the fact that Sym is so shy and the "person" she talks to most is a dead historic figure who only exists insider her head... well, it's a very odd perspective. <br /><br />I will say that there is some great writing in this book, though. The plot and characters just didn't do it for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6389821231743933705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37630750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37630750" />
    <a title="R.J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/969911-r-j"><img alt="R.J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591189619p2/969911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37630750?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.J." href="/user/show/969911-r-j">R.J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer37630750&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37630750" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18284931728899113031">I wavered over whether to choose "I really liked it" or "It was amazing" for this one, but I went with the four stars in the end because it's such a dark book in so many ways that I'm not sure I'd want to read it again. On the other hand, I might just to pick up on all the details I'd missed.<br/><br/>The gorgeous yet narrator-appropriate language in this book, the amount of research that must have gone into it about Antarctica, just staggers me. It is possibly the weirdest book I have read all year, and </span>
  <span id="freeText18284931728899113031" style="display:none">I wavered over whether to choose "I really liked it" or "It was amazing" for this one, but I went with the four stars in the end because it's such a dark book in so many ways that I'm not sure I'd want to read it again. On the other hand, I might just to pick up on all the details I'd missed.<br /><br />The gorgeous yet narrator-appropriate language in this book, the amount of research that must have gone into it about Antarctica, just staggers me. It is possibly the weirdest book I have read all year, and I'm quite sure it has a large number of people who hate it with a rabid passion just because of that, but I didn't find Symone difficult to care about or sympathize with even when she seemed almost impossibly strange and naive, and I definitely wanted to know what Uncle Victor was up to (the author does a very good job, I think, of giving you an ominous squirming feeling right from the beginning that something is Not Quite Right with this whole scenario), so I kept reading.<br /><br />Oh, yeah, and of course I was shipping Symone/Titus. If you don't buy into Titus then you are not going to like this book, but I could readily believe that Symone could retreat into her own head to the degree that Titus became real to her, and yet be intelligent and aware enough not to deep down TRULY believe in his existence (and there are ample clues to that throughout the book -- she really does know better).<br /><br />One possible flaw is that the circumstances in which Symone finds herself, and the characters who surround her, are almost too wildly eccentric to seem real -- and yet it seems like such a quintessentially British approach to storytelling, and I've seen it done so many times even with real people (Gerald Durrell's MY FAMILY AND OTHER ANIMALS comes to mind, or the works of James Herriot) that after a little while I gave up being skeptical and went with it. Your mileage may vary.<br /><br />Anyway, it's weird and brilliant and drives me to total despair when I think of my own attempt at writing a psychologically complex novel with an emotionally repressed heroine, so I have to say I admire it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18284931728899113031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_607555307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/607555307" />
    <a title="Kara Babcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock"><img alt="Kara Babcock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580776593p2/1188122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/607555307?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara Babcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara Babcock" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock">Kara Babcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192726186" href="/book/show/2167592.The_White_Darkness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer607555307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16052992117020912685">I really am not an adventurous person. Moving to England—having never lived on my own before—aside, I’m not the sort of person who enjoys embarking on “expeditions”. I took a trip up to Edinburgh back in October, and that was adventurous enough for me for a few months. These days, a train to Norwich is about as much adventure as I can muster. I read <em>National Geographic</em> and watch the Discovery Channel and soak up all these stories of adventure and exploration vicariously—but I cannot imagine actu</span>
  <span id="freeText16052992117020912685" style="display:none">I really am not an adventurous person. Moving to England—having never lived on my own before—aside, I’m not the sort of person who enjoys embarking on “expeditions”. I took a trip up to Edinburgh back in October, and that was adventurous enough for me for a few months. These days, a train to Norwich is about as much adventure as I can muster. I read <em>National Geographic</em> and watch the Discovery Channel and soak up all these stories of adventure and exploration vicariously—but I cannot imagine actually doing such things myself. I can’t imagine journeying to Antarctica, struggling to survive in a land of endless night and blinding snow … so reading about the plight of Sym Wates was a mixture of shock and awesome.<br><br><em>The White Darkness</em> fulfilled a hunger in me I wasn’t even aware I had. Thanks to the lucrative <em>Twilight</em> and <em>Hunger Games</em> series, it seems like every other young adult novel is some type of escapist, fantasy or science fiction story. I’m the last person who would complain about this. But it’s nice to have an example of a novel that is escapist and fantasy without actually being escapist or fantasy. That is to say, everything in <em>The White Darkness</em> is possible (if slightly implausible). At the same time, it is in the vein of escapism, and it has elements of a fantasy in the way it allows imagination to take over.<br><br>Geraldine McCaughrean’s writing is also amazing. With her simple but elegant descriptions, she manages to create the voice of a fourteen-year-old girl who is isolated but not particularly depressed. McCaughrean’s diction and description communicate a sense of remove from the surrounding world. Sym is bookish and academically inclined; she has friends but is not among the fastest-moving of them. She is a romantic who lives so much in her head that a romantic is about all she can be. Above all else, Sym is interested in polar exploration—so much so that she hears the voice of the late Lawrence “Titus” Oates in her head.<br><br>Sym joins her honourary “Uncle” Victor in a trip to Paris. Her mother can’t join them at the last moment—her passport mysteriously goes missing—so they go to Paris alone. Then—improbably, unlikely, bizarrely—this short trip away from home turns into an expedition to Antarctica, the one place in the world Sym would love to visit. As far away from home, friends, and family as Sym could possibly be, she finds herself among a group of strangers at the edge of the world—and her uncle might just be the most strange of them all.<br><br>From the beginning, McCaughrean insinuates something untoward about Victor’s relationship with Sym. It’s both delicious and unsettling at the same time, because we experience everything from Sym’s perspective of innocence and naivety. Mom can’t come—no passport. Victor eats the SIM card in their mobile phone as a “joke”. He takes Sym shopping for over-priced clothes that make her look more grown-up. As the evidence mounts, McCaughrean lets us draw our own conclusions about what Victor plans to do on this trip to Paris. Is he kidnapping Sym? Is he going to abuse her? Will she manage to figure it out and escape? But at each turn, McCaughrean twists away from the obvious answer.<br><br>It turns out that Victor’s designs on Sym are quite different from the more ordinary tale of sexual abuse at the hands of a family friend. No, though Victor is still guilty of abusing Sym, it’s an abuse that functions on a much more sophisticated level, something that has stretched back far into the past—beyond Sym’s birth, even, to his friendship with her late father. Their unannounced trip to Antarctica is the culmination of Victor’s plans—his schemes, if you will—the confirmation of the conspiracy theory that has captured his mind.<br><br>I love books where some of the most bizarre elements, the elements that you think <em>have</em> to be fictional because they are so outrageous—or just so specific, so convincingly told that they have to be lies—turn out to be the truth. Such is the case with the particularly nineteenth-century flight of fancy that powers the plot of <em>The White Darkness</em>. McCaughrean draws on names, like John Cleeves Symmes, that are probably obscure to the average reader, but are real enough to those with the right interests. She uses real historical people, places, and events to create a backstory, and from there she creates a plot that is fictional—both for us <em>and</em>, sadly, for Sym and her uncle.<br><br>As everything comes crashing down around Sym—both her faith in her uncle and her own certainty in the order of her world—she finds a sudden need to develop agency. Indeed, the first part of the book suffers only in that Sym is a passive protagonist. She just goes along trustingly with Victor, never gainsaying him, never wondering if she shouldn’t find a way to contact her mother. This is frustrating, and I suppose McCaughrean wants it to be that way so that we feel a growing sense of dread as we contemplate what Victor has in store for Sym. Nevertheless, the book doesn’t really come into its own until it lets Sym start acting instead of reacting.<br><br>From that point, <em>The White Darkness</em> turns into a story of survival. Though not my favourite genre, this transition worked for me because of the faith I had built up in Sym, and my need to see Victor laid low. McCaughrean delivers an ending that is satisfactory, albeit somewhat succinct for my tastes. Sym undergoes a crisis both physical and mental, enduring a level of deprivation that I doubt I would ever be able to tolerate.<br><br>It’s possible her imaginary Oates is what helps her through. Oates’ voice runs throughout <em>The White Darkness</em> like an authorial counterpoint, commenting upon events and providing a subconscious voice with which Sym can debate. Oates is funny and charming, warm and prone to reminiscing without being immodest. He is probably the type of adventurer Sym imagines herself being, if she were a man and alive at the turn of the twentieth century…. As it is, Oates becomes the only crutch she can lean on as everything else falls to pieces around her. It’s an interesting, very narrative way of externalizing the ways that people process emotional trauma and abuse.<br><br><em>The White Darkness</em> doesn’t have zombies, or vampires, or giants or werewolves or angels. It doesn’t have a smooth-talking wizard, a mysterious goblin king, or even a Jesus allegory lion. It’s a skilled, highly satisfying combination of a (sadly) ordinary story of obsession and abuse coiled around the extraordinary tale of exploration, survival, and a quest for something that could never be.<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/3.0/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons BY-NC License" width="88" height="31" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238653i/681550.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16052992117020912685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48531479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48531479" />
    <a title="McNeil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2048862-mcneil"><img alt="McNeil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237172088p2/2048862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48531479?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="McNeil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="McNeil" href="/user/show/2048862-mcneil">McNeil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192726186" href="/book/show/2167592.The_White_Darkness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2048862-mcneil?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48531479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7734386035803006517">A gorgeous book. Shocking when someone pure and innocent--not just because she is young--many of her peers are far more worldly-wise than she--is manipulated by those she trusts--she has no idea what is real and what is not. Her whole existence, the whole story she's been told is just based on other people's manipulation of the facts. I'm still not certain whether those who manipulated the facts were conscious that they were doing so. It is yet another great example of the ills of fanaticism, no</span>
  <span id="freeText7734386035803006517" style="display:none">A gorgeous book. Shocking when someone pure and innocent--not just because she is young--many of her peers are far more worldly-wise than she--is manipulated by those she trusts--she has no idea what is real and what is not. Her whole existence, the whole story she's been told is just based on other people's manipulation of the facts. I'm still not certain whether those who manipulated the facts were conscious that they were doing so. It is yet another great example of the ills of fanaticism, no matter what a person is being fanatical about. Fanaticism blinds people and convinces them they are doing the "right" thing even when they are hurting people left and right. They can justify the most heinous behavior, and in this book they sure try. The beautiful and terrifying journey to her truth about her self and her world--to be discovered in the wastes of Antartica, of all places--is one you will not want to miss. The language is wonderful, the character of Sym is so sweet and strong, you will love her and feel with her, and the plot is very exciting. The play of reality vs. imagination is fun, the history lesson is great, and the whole package earns five stars for me, and no reservations in recommending it to youngsters. Probably a PG rating. An example quotation: "It's true: Everyone needs a reason to stay alive--someone who justifies your existence. Someone who loves you. Not beyond all reason. Just loves you. Even just shows an interest. Even someone who doesn't exist, or isn't yours. No, no! They don't even have to love you! They just have to be there to love! Target for your arrows. Magnetic Pole to drag on your compass needle and stop it spinning and spinning and tell you where you're heading and...Someone to soak up all the yearning. That's what I think. That's what I deduce." </span>
  <a data-text-id="7734386035803006517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14107200?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candice M (tinylibrarian)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candice M (tinylibrarian)" href="/user/show/108634-candice-m-tinylibrarian">Candice M (tinylibrarian)</a>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14107200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2011418486492870229">When I think about this book, all I want to do is sigh. Sigh because it was a frustrating read, sigh because of the main character's situation throughout most of the book, and sigh that it won the Printz. <br/><br/>I read it, and I read it fast. I stayed up all night to finish this mother. I was *so* worried about this girl's retarded fate that I couldn't sleep! I needed to find out what happened! So in that sense, yes, it was excellent. In the sense that the story traps you like you've gotten snowed in w</span>
  <span id="freeText2011418486492870229" style="display:none">When I think about this book, all I want to do is sigh. Sigh because it was a frustrating read, sigh because of the main character's situation throughout most of the book, and sigh that it won the Printz. <br /><br />I read it, and I read it fast. I stayed up all night to finish this mother. I was *so* worried about this girl's retarded fate that I couldn't sleep! I needed to find out what happened! So in that sense, yes, it was excellent. In the sense that the story traps you like you've gotten snowed in while you're on holiday in the wilderness. There is no choice. You have to finish. You have to survive.<br /><br />However, I hated myself for caring. I hated myself for my inner optimism which compelled me to keep reading. And maybe that is really where its brilliance lies. That you can hate everything about it but still feel as if you have to finish it.</span>

  <span id="freeText357211874072358579" style="display:none">This book was better than I thought it would be. Set mostly in Antarctica, it starts out like a typical YA novel, with 14 year old Sym telling us how she's bullied at her school in England, is shy, and doesn't fit in. Obsessed with Antarctica and the doomed 1911 expedition, she frequently confides in her imaginary friend, Captain Oates, who was one of the explorers.<br /><br />But when her uncle Victor takes her on a trip to Antarctica, it soon turns into something more horrible than she ever suspected it would be. There were times I thought Sym was a bit too naive, even for 14. However, I think she had to be so that the plot would progress. And maybe she did want to think the best of those around her. (I was pretty cynical at 14, myself.) The story got pretty dark towards the end, and had a realistic ending. An unusual YA read.</span>

And I can often say the same for a book; I can tell I love it within the first twenty pages or so. But The White Darkness took me until page 73 to get really hooked. And then I couldn’t put it down.   <span id="freeText8700335787959564956" style="display:none">I have a friend who says she can tell if she’ll love a movie with the first ten minutes. And I can often say the same for a book; I can tell I love it within the first twenty pages or so. But The White Darkness took me until page 73 to get really hooked. And then I couldn’t put it down. It’s about a teenage girl, Symone, who gets her dream vacation: a trip to Antarctica. She is obsessed with Antarctica and one of its brave explorers, Captain Oates from Scott’s doomed expedition to the South Pole. She always has been. And her Uncle Victor has always supported her. But there’s something off about Uncle Victor. He’s even more obsessed with Antarctica than Sym. This is a devastating explosion of a plot that delivers aftershock after rolling aftershock.</span>

<div id="review_2591035461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591035461" />
    <a title="P. Kirby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112326-p-kirby"><img alt="P. Kirby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442534274p2/5112326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591035461?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P. Kirby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="P. Kirby" href="/user/show/5112326-p-kirby">P. Kirby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112326-p-kirby?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112326-p-kirby?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112326-p-kirby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591035461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11748038136279360048"><b>This novel gave me frostbite by proxy.</b><br/><br/>Much younger me loved the cold, but somewhere along the road of life, my inner heater started failing, and now 60-degrees F gives me chilblains. Thank the dear and fuzzy wuzzy lord for intrepid explorers and filmmakers who bring visions of Antarctica into the warm comfort of my living room. Because no place is gorgeous enough to justify skin freezing on contact with the air.<br/><br/>Fourteen-year-old Sym is in love with an older man--sort of--Titus Oates, a member of</span>
  <span id="freeText11748038136279360048" style="display:none"><b>This novel gave me frostbite by proxy.</b><br /><br />Much younger me loved the cold, but somewhere along the road of life, my inner heater started failing, and now 60-degrees F gives me chilblains. Thank the dear and fuzzy wuzzy lord for intrepid explorers and filmmakers who bring visions of Antarctica into the warm comfort of my living room. Because no place is gorgeous enough to justify skin freezing on contact with the air.<br /><br />Fourteen-year-old Sym is in love with an older man--sort of--Titus Oates, a member of famous explorer's Captain Robert Falcon Scott's doomed Antarctic trip. Titus, who froze to death on the 1911 trip, along with the rest of the team, has captivated Sym's imagination and as an imaginary friend, fends off her loneliness. Painfully shy, hard-of-hearing and wearing hearing aids, Sym is friendless and a target for bullies. A few years before, her father, who she believes never liked her anyway, died of a mysterious infection that destroyed his sanity. Sym and her mother survive financially through the benevolence of her father's friend, Uncle Victor. Victor, an eccentric, is a nutter who believes that lost civilizations, more advanced than ours, live in Earth's hollow depths beneath Antarctica.<br /><br />Sym and Victor's adventure begins with an innocuous trip to Paris. Sym's mother is supposed to come along, but at the last minute, before boarding the train, finds her passport is missing. It seems innocuous enough, but an astute reader will quickly start to smell a rat--a rat named Uncle Victor.<br /><br />After a day or so in Paris, Victor announces that their trip will extend farther south. Sym assumes this means the Mediterranean, perhaps. Instead, it turns out Victor has booked them passage with an expensive travel outfit that takes people on short trips to Antarctica.<br /><br />But for Uncle Victor, simply being in Antarctica isn't enough. Through a series of unfortunate events, he acquires/steals an arctic Humvee-vehicle and drags Sym on a grueling, life-threatening trek across the bleak ice in search of a portal into the Earth's hollows. What follows is a brutal journey, physically and emotionally, through a landscape inhospitable to nearly all life, and death to humans. As the trip unfolds, Sym, who worships her Uncle almost as much as imaginary Titus, learns how misplaced her admiration is and how deeply a person can be betrayed.<br /><br />My reactions to the story vacillated between irritation at Sym's naivete and then fury at Victor's lunacy and abuse. Sym's unflagging belief in Victor's intelligence is annoying, and yet, realistic for a sheltered, awkward child.<br /><br />The thing is, people, even adult people, will often believe that someone is the strongest, smartest, most wonderful person, if the person brags enough. Case in point, one of my husband's co-workers. The man, let's call him Bob, is mediocre at best. But he carries on and on, telling everyone how busy he is, how much he does for the company. And...a number of employees believe his narrative, agreeing that his inability to get promoted is "unfair" and the result of cruel biases against Bob. (Unfortunately for Bob, he's too dimwitted to sell his greatness to management, so his fan club consists of fellow technicians and admin staff.)<br /><br />Point is, if Bob can get adults to believe his narrative of greatness, it's no surprise that a child would fall for the same from a "respected" adult/parent-figure.<br /><br /><i>The White Darkness</i> seems to be a love or hate-it book, but my reaction is solidly centrist. The journey across the ice is enthralling; the lack of significant romance, a relief; and the emotional landscape just as brutal as Antarctica's. I never felt manipulated, but I never really got the "feelz," either.<br /><br />36 stars. (Bumping up to four stars because the story's original premise and locale are memorable.)<br /><br />(Library book)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11748038136279360048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4596580450976503891">A young girl named Symone is taken without her mother's permission by her "uncle" on a trip to the Antarctic. Uncle is obsessed with the idea of a world or worlds within the Earth and is convinced that the access portal to these worlds lies at the South Pole. Sym is a whole lot naive and completely too trusting of this uncle but as the story goes on she becomes more and more aware of how crazy her uncle is. The trip is dangerous with hazards you can't even imagine and is driven by the obsessed m</span>
  <span id="freeText4596580450976503891" style="display:none">A young girl named Symone is taken without her mother's permission by her "uncle" on a trip to the Antarctic. Uncle is obsessed with the idea of a world or worlds within the Earth and is convinced that the access portal to these worlds lies at the South Pole. Sym is a whole lot naive and completely too trusting of this uncle but as the story goes on she becomes more and more aware of how crazy her uncle is. The trip is dangerous with hazards you can't even imagine and is driven by the obsessed madman and fed into by some con men who think Uncle is rich. What they don't know is that he's spent every penny on this last chance to find "Symme's Hole". Young Sym has to find a way to save herself and her crazy uncle in the middle of the Antarctic plateau.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4596580450976503891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19657883" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19657883" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41583-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414511167p2/41583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19657883?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/41583-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">8th grade and up</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19657883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer382024021503964914">"What! Whoa!" was the chorus running through my head as I read this highly unusual story, this year's Printz Award winner. Although it took a while to get going, it quickly morphed into a layered mystery, narrated by 14-year-old British girl Sym, who accompanies her Uncle Victor (and her imaginary friend, the Artic explorer "Titus" Oates) on a trip to Paris which turns into a trip to Antarctica (!!) and a survival story unlike any other. Pair with "Life As We Knew It" for two great survival-girl</span>
  <span id="freeText382024021503964914" style="display:none">"What! Whoa!" was the chorus running through my head as I read this highly unusual story, this year's Printz Award winner. Although it took a while to get going, it quickly morphed into a layered mystery, narrated by 14-year-old British girl Sym, who accompanies her Uncle Victor (and her imaginary friend, the Artic explorer "Titus" Oates) on a trip to Paris which turns into a trip to Antarctica (!!) and a survival story unlike any other. Pair with "Life As We Knew It" for two great survival-girl protagonists, but only if you really, REALLY want to appreciate the comforts of civilization.<br /><br />Incredible writing and imagery, too. Favorite quotes (advance apologies, I had a lot):<br /><br />"Like everything perfect, he set up a ferocious pain inside me -- a flickering, griping sort of pain, because nothing as marvelous as that is ever within reach, is it? Nothing as beautiful can ever last."<br /><br />"'Give my love to...' I began to say, but I could think of no one in England who wanted it."<br /><br />"When Titus speaks, I can hear every word. For me, that's like when the optician slides home the right lens and all the e's and g's and o's and c's become perfectly clear again and it isn't a struggle, even to read the bottom-most line...His voice touches places inside me like someone moving through a house, flicking light switches...No peering into corners for what's been said."<br /><br />"For some crime committed by my ancestors in the dark and forgotten days, I came into the world already tarred and feathered. With shyness. It hurts terribly -- every bit as much as hot tar choking every pore -- and I wish I could be rid of it. But it hurts a lot less than having someone try and <i>peel the shyness off.</i> That's like being flayed alive." <br /><br />"The interior? That empty, featureless plateau, rising up and up to high-altitude nothingness with no feature fixing its center -- it mesmerized me. The idea of it took me in thrall. It was so empty, so blank, so clean, so dead. Surely, if I was ever to set foot down there, even I might finally exist. Surely, in this Continent of Nothingness, anything -- anyone -- had to be hugely alive by comparison!"<br /><br />"There are things roaming around inside my head as clever as Theseus in the Labyrinth. It's just that nobody ever gave them the necessary piece of string, so they'll never find their way out."<br /><br />"You have to do things sometimes to strengthen your courage muscles." <br /><br />"Every crime like this needs someone like me to look away and say nothing."<br /><br />"'Don't struggle too hard to understand people, Sym. They're hideously complicated. Unhappy people do the oddest, most terrible things, just trying to keep despair at bay. All you have to do is accept them...go around them...take evasive action.'"<br /><br />"'All right, all right, Titus. But it's like throwing dinner rolls at a charging rhino is all I'm saying.'"<br /><br />"That's how it's done, you see. It's the same way people get horses out of burning buildings. When the whole world's on fire around you, you use a blindfold. Everyone needs someone like Titus for a blindfold." <br /><br />"It's true: Everyone needs a reason to stay alive -- someone who justifies your existence. Someone who loves you. Not beyond all reaon. Just loves you. Even just shows an interest. Even someone who doesn't exist, or isn't yours. No, no! They don't even have to love you! They just have to be there to love! Target for your arrows. Magnetic Pole to drag on your compass needle and stop it spinning and tell you where you're heading and...Someone to soak up all the yearning. That's what I think." <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="382024021503964914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_13551742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13551742" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/164794-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183308121p2/164794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13551742?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/164794-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13551742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7047659812878325491">In this brilliantly crafted story of madness and despair comes the story of teenage Sym who is whisked away from her normal teenage anxieties to face the bleak desolation of Antarctica and her uncle's obsession. Sym is a normal British teen, unpopular boys and the butt of many jokes with her friends. Her father has died rather tragically, but Sym finds solace by insulating herself in a fictional world where her principal friend is an incarnation of Captain Lawerence Oates, who lead an ill-fated </span>
  <span id="freeText7047659812878325491" style="display:none">In this brilliantly crafted story of madness and despair comes the story of teenage Sym who is whisked away from her normal teenage anxieties to face the bleak desolation of Antarctica and her uncle's obsession. Sym is a normal British teen, unpopular boys and the butt of many jokes with her friends. Her father has died rather tragically, but Sym finds solace by insulating herself in a fictional world where her principal friend is an incarnation of Captain Lawerence Oates, who lead an ill-fated expedition to the South Pole. Titus, as Sym lovingly refers to him, is her constant and only companion in her journey to bottom of herself and to the bottom of the earth. At no point do any of doomed characters warrant sympathy, yet this sad story is completely compelling in it's wonderful description of the slow self-destruction of the obsessed mind. <br />It is very rare that I quote a passage of the book, but so sharp is the writing in this book, which captivates the reader, that I find myself lost in the words. From page 81 on, "Why, when we overflew the coast, were there turquoise sculptures of ice rolling over and over in waves of indigo? It terrifies me, the sea. I know it would kill me if it could. I think this whole continent would kill us if it could once sink its teeth into us... And yet,I've never seen anywhere so beautiful, so marvelous. " <br />Consumed by her demented uncle's vision, Sym finds herself slowly self destructing as the world she knows slips away from her fingers. This reminds me of the amazing movie, Mosquito Coast, in which Harrison Ford's character is so hell-bent on escaping the confines of the modern world, that he drags his family along his descent into self-preservation and ultimately madness. <br />Equally challenging and engaging, you never know where this story is going, much like the Life of Pi from a few years ago. Take the time to emerge yourself into this amazingly dark, yet blindingly white world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7047659812878325491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47679834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47679834" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1313520-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257953885p2/1313520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47679834?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1313520-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47679834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9294018553321195741">This was a very good book from a literary standpoint. It is however, not a "fun" read. It is a Printz award winner for the best book of the year for young adults, and deservedly so. <br/><br/>It is a tale of a teen from England who gets taken on a surprise trip to Antartica with her uncle. Symone's (Sym) story quickly turns into a survival tale, as she deals with an increasingly manic uncle.<br/><br/>What helps Sym get through is her imaginary relationship with a long dead artic explorer. This character is more rea</span>
  <span id="freeText9294018553321195741" style="display:none">This was a very good book from a literary standpoint. It is however, not a "fun" read. It is a Printz award winner for the best book of the year for young adults, and deservedly so. <br /><br />It is a tale of a teen from England who gets taken on a surprise trip to Antartica with her uncle. Symone's (Sym) story quickly turns into a survival tale, as she deals with an increasingly manic uncle.<br /><br />What helps Sym get through is her imaginary relationship with a long dead artic explorer. This character is more real to her than most of the people she is traveling with.<br /><br />Sym is (justifiably) very naive about what is acutally happening during this trip. She fails to question her "genius" uncle when the spontaneous trip to Paris (which her mother missed because of a lost passport) turns into an Antartic expidition. She blindly accepts all the assurances of her uncle, even as they become more suspect to a reader. On one hand, Sym's cluelessness is irritating. On the other hand, as we learn more about how Sym's uncle has manipulated her all of her life with an increasingly disturbing series of lies, her ignorance and the choices she makes because of it become plausable.<br /><br />Eventually, pulling on strength she didn't know she had, Sym opens her eyes to her uncle's maniacal plans. She is able to resist him, and more importantly, survive the Antarctic expidition. <br /><br />In many ways, Sym's uncle is one of the most disturbing characters I've encountered in a long time. Sanity of all the characters is in question throughout the tale. It's an excellent read, but not one to pick up in a blue mood.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9294018553321195741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/735516430?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eilonwy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eilonwy" href="/user/show/17237503-eilonwy">Eilonwy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17237503-eilonwy?shelf=well-written">well-written</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer735516430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7239859625392739028"><blockquote>14-year-old Symone Wates is more than a bit socially awkward (her obvious hearing aids don't help). But thanks to her obsession with the doomed Scott Antarctic Expedition, she's got a pretty solid relationship with Lawrence "Titus" Oates, a member of the team -- even if he does exist only in her head. When family friend "Uncle" Victor, who shares her obsession, takes Sym on a surprise trip to actual Antarctica, her knowledge of the geography and what it takes to survive will be put to the test a</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7239859625392739028" style="display:none"><blockquote>14-year-old Symone Wates is more than a bit socially awkward (her obvious hearing aids don't help). But thanks to her obsession with the doomed Scott Antarctic Expedition, she's got a pretty solid relationship with Lawrence "Titus" Oates, a member of the team -- even if he does exist only in her head. When family friend "Uncle" Victor, who shares her obsession, takes Sym on a surprise trip to actual Antarctica, her knowledge of the geography and what it takes to survive will be put to the test as she finds herself in circumstances more terrifying than she ever imagined.</blockquote><br />I have mixed feelings about this book.<br /> <br /><u>The Good</u>: I really liked Sym, and found both her voice and her awkwardness entirely believable; her isolation and social discomfort felt genuine rather than like a mere plot device (as in too many other books). The balance between her relative immaturity and her curiosity about the more adult things her schoolmates were growing into rang absolutely true. Her internal relationship with Titus was very well done, as well, as she's able to feel safe in a sort-of-close friendship with a man who is clearly too old for her and a bit distant about the whole thing himself. The writing is both beautiful and gripping, and the story moves at a good pace. I can see why this book got rave reviews when it was published (2005) and won the Printz Award. <br /> <br /><u>The Not-So-Good</u>: Some of the twists are a little too obvious from an adult perspective. Younger readers might find some of the revelations to be a surprise, but I didn't (except for one, which was very creepily brought to light; the minus is that I don't quite believe it). And when Uncle Victor's actual reason for the Antarctic trip was revealed, I nearly threw the book across the room because I found it far too preposterous. But I kept reading, and I think it was worth it. <br /> <br /><u>The Warnin</u>g: This is one of those books which casts doubt on trusting other people, so it might not be a good match for any kid who already worries about that sort of thing or has a vivid imagination. And in light of that, I found the very ending to be just a tad too rosy. <br /> <br />Overall, this was a captivating, vivid read, so if you're in the mood for a sort of adventure/suspense novel, I would recommend it, with the reservations noted above. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7239859625392739028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20664304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20664304" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/260586-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386712907p2/260586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20664304?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/260586-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/260586-krista?shelf=teen-fiction">teen-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20664304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14467210951485932760">Fourteen year-old Sym seems to be trapped in her own mind, her deafness, shyness, and social naiveté make her an outcast at school. Her father's death has made her mother distant and invited her eclectic uncle into bring the family out of a financial burden. However, when her uncle, who feeds her love for all things about Antarctica, encourages the family to take a trip, Sym gets whisked away from her mother and thrown into a dangerous adventure in the icy continent with her uncle. His drive for</span>
  <span id="freeText14467210951485932760" style="display:none">Fourteen year-old Sym seems to be trapped in her own mind, her deafness, shyness, and social naiveté make her an outcast at school. Her father's death has made her mother distant and invited her eclectic uncle into bring the family out of a financial burden. However, when her uncle, who feeds her love for all things about Antarctica, encourages the family to take a trip, Sym gets whisked away from her mother and thrown into a dangerous adventure in the icy continent with her uncle. His drive for fame and an uncertain "hole to the center of the earth" forces Sym to confront painful memories and rethink herself, her beliefs, and her future.<br /><br />The themes of isolation, power, and manipulation, as well as similar plot developments, make the work a modern day companion to fellow British author Joseph Conrad's Heart of Darkness. However, the lack of character development, and the disappointing flat dimension of both the protagonist and antagonist do not elevate this novel to the greatness of Conrad's work. While the stream of conscious formula may be alluring to teen readers, the uses of flashbacks provide little in the way of interesting or significant context towards the novel's current action.<br /><br />Definitely not a book for a reluctant reader. The slow pacing and the repetitive nature of the prose make for an infuriating struggle to remain attentive to the already complex novel. I don't understand how or why the novel is award worthy, especially considering that in the resurrected popularity of Pullman's The Golden Compass, this novel's plot seems entirely unoriginal. The only positive comment I can make about the novel is the description of the Antarctic setting. Its monotony can make one understand how the characters were driven to madness.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14467210951485932760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14235207086772470181" style="display:none">This was on the required reading list for YA Lit. This was the worst book I read all semester, and I'm sad that this is the last book on my list. I might have to squeeze another book into my schedule just to get the taste out of my mouth before the end of the semester. End on a good note. This book was long and boring. The author used 370 pages when 200 would have been fine. I kept waiting to get into it or to care at all for the story or the characters, but it just never happened. I started to like Sigurd, but then his character completely flip-flopped and started acting lame in the last 10% of the book. When the book wasn't boring, it was confusing. I also found the uncle unbelievably unbelievable. <br /><br />The one redeeming quality of the book was some of the figurative language the author used.   <span id="freeText2838274101099812131" style="display:none">I absolutley love this book. Yet again Geraldine Mccaughrean has produced a book for the young adult market which surpassess anything else on the reading shelves. Sym is a teenage girl going through teen things until her uncle decides to take her to Paris or so she and everyone elso thinks, that is until she arrives in the antarctic.   <span id="freeText9922209064708068573" style="display:none">Interesting plot twists and an author who really likes poetic justice. It does seem a little unbelievable that the girl who couldn't speak a coherent sentence becomes vindictive and even flirty within the course of a week. Just loves you. Even just shows an interest. Even someone who doesn't exist, or isn't yours. No, no! They don't even have to love you! They just have to be there to love...someone to soak up all the yearning."</span>

<div id="review_2049041492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049041492" />
    <a title="Josephine Sorrell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2954128-josephine-sorrell"><img alt="Josephine Sorrell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479397099p2/2954128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049041492?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josephine Sorrell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josephine Sorrell" href="/user/show/2954128-josephine-sorrell">Josephine Sorrell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049041492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7397730448358601960">This was recommended for my book challenge Antarctica read. The cover looked intriguing as did the reviews and it won Printz award in 2008 so it must be fabulous. I slogged through it, temped to skip the italicised ramblings of imaginary character or should I say dead person Titus, in Symn's head.<br/><br/>The saga opens with a nice surprise: "Uncle" Victor Briggs, a family friend, has planned an impromptu weekend for Sym Wates and her mother in France. Sym is thrilled. So thrilled, in fact, that she's ab</span>
  <span id="freeText7397730448358601960" style="display:none">This was recommended for my book challenge Antarctica read. The cover looked intriguing as did the reviews and it won Printz award in 2008 so it must be fabulous. I slogged through it, temped to skip the italicised ramblings of imaginary character or should I say dead person Titus, in Symn's head.<br /><br />The saga opens with a nice surprise: "Uncle" Victor Briggs, a family friend, has planned an impromptu weekend for Sym Wates and her mother in France. Sym is thrilled. So thrilled, in fact, that she's able to overlook the fact that Victor steals her mother's passport, leaving her behind in England. Victor's next surprise: Their final destination is actually the South Pole. As in Antarctica. Symn has always been fascinated with this end of the earth wonder. Victor claims this has all been deemed ok by Symn's mother.<br /><br />The reader may wonder why Symn so easily agrees to this bizarre and costly adventure. Well, Sym doesn't have many friends, for one thing, and for another, her father recently died from a grisly illness and It's time for a change. Throw caution to the wind and Let's - shake - it - up Uncle Victor style. <br /><br />At the South Pole, Sym and Victor set up base camp with a travel outfit called Pengwings. There, they join forces with a pair of con men, Manfred and Sigurd Bruch, who are posing as a Viking filmmaker and his son. <br /><br />As the plot thickens may I say, Victor blows up the plane and drugs and almost everyone at camp so the four can steal off in the night. Victor's secret agenda is to find Symmes's Hole, an imaginary portal to the center of earth that he's been obsessed with for years. Manfred and Sigurd's secret agenda is to steal Victor's money... yadda yadda yadda...<br /><br />Now, find our characters on a harrowing car ride across thin ice, Manfred admits to his con. Victor, who is fully off his rocker, just murders him and keeps on spinning. For Sym, the expedition goes from bad to worse when Victor admits to a series of betrayals (including murdering Sym's father and swindling her family out of a lot of money) and sends her and Sigurd out in front of the vehicle to scout for cracks in the ice. To save themselves, Sigurd manages to steal the vehicle, leaving Sym and Victor for dead in the snow. <br /><br />Soon after all that, good old Uncle Victor throws himself down into the abyss he takes to be Symmes's Hole. Did I say this guy is off his rocker? <br /><br />Sym's learned a lot of difficult truths about Victor just before she watches him plunge to his death. Overwhelmed by her feelings, she wants nothing so much as to lie down in the snow and die. Dead Titus manages to talk her out of this terrible plan and helps lead her to the nearest thing to safety. Sigurd. vehicle has stalled out in the snow and seeing Symn he takes her in, shoots her up with some adrenaline from the first aid kit, and she comes back to life.<br /><br />Desperately, Sym blows up the broken-down vehicle. No one sees it, but they're rescued anyway. On the long boat ride home, as she recovers from her arduous journey, Sym learns she has an admirer: Mike, one of her fellow travelers from the Pengwings tour. Much to her surprise, he asks her out. She's not ready to date yet—she's only fourteen—but she knows she will be someday soon.<br /><br />The ending was lame and dissatisfying.<br /><br />But I have an entry for my challenge. Not all is lost. Smiling</span>
  <a data-text-id="7397730448358601960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_279382605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279382605" />
    <a title="Marta Boksenbaum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2145510-marta-boksenbaum"><img alt="Marta Boksenbaum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1279369972p2/2145510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279382605?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marta Boksenbaum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marta Boksenbaum" href="/user/show/2145510-marta-boksenbaum">Marta Boksenbaum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2145510-marta-boksenbaum?shelf=teen-lit">teen-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279382605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4489229564997020755">This novel follows quiet and shy Sym as her Antarctic-obsessed Uncle Victor whirls her off on a surprise journey to the frozen wilderness and the events that lead her to a survival adventure that parallels her personal hero and imaginary friend Captain Oates’ expedition in the South Pole. Sym is so shy that she only talks to her imagined love Captain Oates that she built up from her reading on the expedition. The novel centers on her internal dialogue though conversations with this character. He</span>
  <span id="freeText4489229564997020755" style="display:none">This novel follows quiet and shy Sym as her Antarctic-obsessed Uncle Victor whirls her off on a surprise journey to the frozen wilderness and the events that lead her to a survival adventure that parallels her personal hero and imaginary friend Captain Oates’ expedition in the South Pole. Sym is so shy that she only talks to her imagined love Captain Oates that she built up from her reading on the expedition. The novel centers on her internal dialogue though conversations with this character. Her father’s friend Victor who she refers to as “uncle” takes her with him as he fanatically seeks a revolutionary discovery, taking them deep into the gaping desert of Antarctica and endangering their lives and forcing Sym to take control of her own life. <br />The book includes a great deal of description of Antarctica, in which the land almost becomes another character in the novel, and with which the protagonist develops a relationship. McCaughrean uses imagery as well as personification in Sym’s first encounter with the icy land: “Below us was a curding of sea ice--here, there, and everywhere--a mosaic of white puzzle pieces saying, ‘Solve me! Solve me!”-the makings of a self-assembly world waiting to be glued together’ (p. 73). McCaughrean uses language imaginatively to juxtapose the beauty and the danger of Antarctica, describing the precipitation at one point of the journey as “frozen dew”, with which the characters were “…bombarded with rainbows, falling from an infinite height, dazzling [them] with iridescent spears and darts and cataracts of cascading color. Some of the particles were so sharp that they embedded themselves in our suits like Lilliputian arrows” (p. 210) However, as well written as the description of the setting was, it was so extensive that I quickly grew weary of it and wished the book would just end already. As I was reading, I was aware that it was included to show the reader how expansive Antarctica is and how tedious the journey of the characters is. However, I did not have the stamina and found that I had to push myself to finish the book. <br />I also found Sym’s voice to be overly naive in places and unbelievingly mature in others. She is obviously an attractive girl who happens to be incredibly shy, but she is not stupid or insecure. So, her denial of Uncle Victor’s unstable obsession of exploration, and the attention of men of which she seemed completely unaware became irritating.<br />Although I did not enjoy this novel I could see others enjoying it more than I did. I think a reader who would like this book might be someone who can relate to the painful feeling of being shy and unable to interact with other people or someone who is interested in Antarctica and survival books. The story is incredibly unlikely, but the descriptions of Antarctica are beautifully written and the interaction of the protagonist with her imaginary friend is interesting.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4489229564997020755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
